This uses the informal "you" (vosotros) since it seems like the speaker is addressing a group of people directly. "Quiero" means "I want," and "vean" comes from the verb "ver" meaning "to see." <NL> - "this is" is translated as "esto es" in Spanish. "Esto" means "this" and "es" is the third person singular form of "ser," which is used for permanent or inherent characteristics. <NL> - "Fuku, a young female" is translated as "Fuku, una joven mujer" in Spanish. "Una" means "a" and "joven" means "young." "Mujer" means "woman," but since Fuku is a name of a person, it's clear that we're referring to a female human being. <NL> - "and she is quietly playing" is translated as "y está jugando tranquilamente" in Spanish. "Y" means "and." The verb "está" (third person singular form of "estar") is used here because "playing" refers to an action that is currently taking place, and "tranquilamente" means "quietly" or "calmly." <NL> - "with water" is translated as "con el agua" in Spanish. "Con" means "with," "el" is the definite article "the," and "agua" means "water."
